W H A T DO W E K N O W  ABO U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 73
INTRODUCTION
Volcanism is an imposing natural phenomenon amazing the 
imagination with giant flares of flashes and eruptions, deafening 
thunder and explosions. Only few people know that so-called 
magmatic volcanoes have less eminent relatives -  mud volcanoes
Mud volcanism is one of the most unusual and interesting 
natural phenomena that is marked by variability of forms and a 
specific character of activity. For this reason mud volcanoes for a 
long time have been in the focus of travellers, researchers and 
tourists. Tthe publications about fire eruptions of mud volcanoes 
that impress with the magnitude and mysteriousness of the 
phenomenon date back to ancient times. As far back as in the V 
century Azerbaijan’s mud volcanoes attracted attention of diplomat 
Priscus of Panium and of Arabian travelers Masoudi and Al-Gamati 
in the X-XIII. Masoudi in his tractate “Meadows of Gold and Mines 
of Gem Stones” described one of eruptions that occurred in the 
Caspian Sea in the group of volcanic islands of the Baku 
Archipelago.
The first information of mud volcanoes eruptions near Baku 
were published in 1828 (Gamba, Deikham).
Significant contribution into the beginning of the systematic 
studies of mud volcanoes was made by such scientists as
G.W.Abich, D.V.Golubyatnikov, K.V.Kharichkov, I.M.Gubkin,
E.A.Shteber, S.A.Kovalevski, V.A.Gorin and et al.
Over the last decades mud volcanoes were profoundly studied 
by Azerbaijan geologists: A.A.Yakubov, A.A.Alizadeh,
Ad.A.Aliyev, R.R.Rakhmanov, Z.A.Buniat-Zadeh, F.G.Dadashev, 
Sh.F.Mehtiyev, M.M.Zeynalov et al.
Today we have significant amount of scientific information 
about mud volcanoes. However it is possible to say that this 
information unlike magmatic volcanoes does not go beyond local 
boundaries and for this reason readers far outside the areas of 
development of mud volcanoes are not familiar with them.
In this book we tried to tell about mud volcanoes, regularities of
74
their occurrence, mechanism of formation, character of activity, 
composition of depth material produced by them and role of 
volcanoes in addressing different fundamental and application tasks 
in the most popular and intelligible form for a wide circle of 
readers.
The book is rich in bright photos of different forms of activities 
of mud volcanoes (photos by Ad. A. Aliyev).
Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev W H A T DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 75
Photo 1. Natural gas vent seep Yanardağ
Fires attracted people from old times and they were worshipped 
which is evidenced by numerous fire temples Nush-Jan-Tepe, 
Adurgushnaep, Surakhany, Pirallahi,. Hovsany, Shakhdagh and 
others. The history of fire worshipping in Azerbaijan and adjacent 
parts of Iran dates back centuries.
According to historical notes as far back as six centuries B.C. 
the fire cult was widely known in the Absheron Peninsula. Here, a 
well-known temple of Ateshgah is preserved not far from the 
railway station of Surakhany near the former V. A.Kokarev plant.
I. MUD VOLCANOES AND ZOROASTRIANISM
The area of Azerbaijan is exceptionally rich in numerous natural 
gas seeps, among which natural gas fires are distinguished, such as 
Yanar Dag in the Absheron Peninsula, etc. Gas flares are especially 
impressive during eruptions of mud volcanoes (photo 1,2).
76 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 2. Gas flame on a volcano
At that time dead fire worshippers were burned in this temple 
and their ash was sent to India. The temple was ruined in the VII 
century, but it was restored later and fire burned there till the end of 
the XIX century. The last priests of the temple lived there in the 70s 
of the XIX century and worshipped the eternal fire that was 
supplied there by clay pipes from the nearest natural gas surface 
vents. Grey bearded people with dark faces and flame tails painted 
by sienna on the forehead and cheeks three times a day prayed the 
God of fire and life.
Numerous fire worshippers from Bagdad and Bukhara, Khoresm 
and Arabia, India, China and even from Japan flowed into 
Azerbaijan that became a center, a Mecca of fire worshipping 
(photo 3).
In pre-Islam Iran the fire cult had a primary significance over 
many centuries. The name of the first wearer of crown (tsar) was 
Atrapat which means “protected by fire”. The role of fire was 
especially important in the Sasonide period when Zoroastrianism 
(fire worshipping) was founded. Zarathustra, the founder of
Zoroastrianism, as some researchers believe was bom in the 
Southern Azerbaijan.

Zoroastrianism over 3-4 centuries played a significant role even 
after the Arab Conquest. Many works of the Zoroastrianism 
literature were written in this period.
Such great Azeris as Nizami, Hagani, Nasimi dedicated their 
inspired lines to Zoroastrianism. Nizami and Hagani cautioned 
against fire worshipping, while Hasimi glorified fire almost in every 
poem.
We have all reasons to believe that gas flames of the mud 
volcanoes played not the last role in the emergence of one of the 
main world’s religions.

II. WHAT ARE MUD VOLCANOES AND THEIR 
SPECIFIC FEATURES?
Photo 4. Mud volcano Touragai. General view
Usually in the modem terrain mud volcanoes form more or less 
large highlands on the land surface that often have flat and cone 
shape. Morphologically they mainly have a shape of a truncated 
cone with relative elevation of up to 400 m and resemble magmatic 
volcanoes (photo 4). The diameter of the base of volcanoes ranges 
from 100 m to 3-4 km, the shape of the top of the volcanoes ranges 
from convex-plane or shield-like to deeply sunken like a caldera. 
The crater diameter sometimes exceeds 500-600 m. Usually its 
position corresponds to the central part of a volcano and represents 
the end of the channel of volcanic vent that links the source of the 
volcano with the earth’s surface. Mud volcanic breccia is thrown 
out through the crater. It is accompanied by gas and mineralized 
water stream. Relative elevations and the shape of the slopes of the 
volcano crater depend both on its activity and the character of 
erupted masses (photo 5).
W H A T DO W E K N O W  A B O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 79
Photo 5. Mud volcano Lökbatan. Eruption on October 7, 1977
So, mud volcanoes are essentially peculiar apparatuses for 
emission of gas and mud volcanic breccia to surface from relatively 
shallow depths (5-12 km). During emptions also angular rock 
fragments of different compositions and age sometimes reaching 
several meters in the cross section are thrown out of volcanoes with 
the clay. Their amount is approximately 10-15%. The majority of 
the products of activities of mud volcanoes are thrown out 
periodically during eruption paroxysms. In the periods between 
them the crater field of a volcano is covered by numerous parasitic 
microforms -  active salses, gryphons, hills that produce gas, 
mineral water mostly with an oil film and silty (mount) mud of 
different consistency (photo 6,7).
The bodies of volcanoes are created by superposition of breccia 
during numerous eruptions. The shape of a volcano depends on the 
consistency of breccia. If it is dense the volcano has a shape of a 
cone with a steep slope; if breccia has high water content the 
volcanoes usually have a low and flattened shape with a flat saucer­
like crater (photo 8).
80 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A A Feyzullayev
Photo 7. Gryphons producing gas, water and mud
Photo 8. Mud salse
The flows of mud volcanic breccia like the crater plateau are 
main morphological element of mud volcanic relief their shape 
depends on the character of the bed, surface slope and breccia 
composition (photo 9).
During strong eruptions mud volcanic breccia usually flows out 
in the form of thick fan-shaped or tongue-like streams with width of 
several hundreds of meters and length of over a kilometer. Their 
thickness reaches 10-12 m. The breccia flowing from the crater 
funnel sometimes forms tongues of a peculiar shape. Moreover, the 
streams of volcanic breccia sometimes occupy significant area. The 
area of distribution of breccia cover on Ajiveli and Solakhai 
volcanoes (Azerbaijan) is 45 and 58 km2, respectively, with an 
average thickness of breccia of 100 m. The thickness of the cover in 
the central part of a volcano sometimes reaches 800-1000 m.
82_____________________________ Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A ^ f eyzullayev
Photo 9. Volcanic mudflow
The amount of solid product produced by volcanoes is also 
significant (photo 10). Approximate amounts of mud volcano 
material produced by several large volcanoes are provided below. 
Azerbaijan: Ahtarma-Pashaly -  16 bln.m3; Ayrantokan -  2.4 
bln.m3; Otmanbozdagh -  1.2 bln.m3; B.Kyanizadag -  735 mln.m3. 
Turkmenistan: Barsa-Telmes -  3.5 bn.m3. The Kerch Peninsula: 
Djautepe -  55 mln.m3. Georgia: Akhtala- 350 thous.m3 (photo 11).

Islands, banks, shoals and underwater ranges are formed in the 
result of mud volcanism. There are 9 islands of mud volcanic origin 
(Zenbil, Gil, Khara-Zirya, Garasu, Sengi-Mugan, etc.) and 
numerous underwater banks. Subsea eruptions of volcanic breccia 
form vast mantles on the sea bed. The depth of underwater banks 
ranges from several meters to 900 m, their cone height is also 
variable. Some onshore volcanoes are up to 400 m and higher. A 
new large sea volcano was found in 2000 in the south of the Baku 
Archipelago (photo 12, 13, 14, Corthay, Aliyev).
Photo 14. Underwater volcano in the Southern Caspian Sea

III. WHIMS OF MUD VOLCANOES
3.1. MUD VOLCANOES - WHERE ARE YOU?
Mud volcanism is a natural phenomenon of a global scale. It can 
be found in 36 countries of the world and also in the deep water part 
of the Caspian, Black and Mediterranean Seas (figure 1).
MUD VOLCANOES OF THE WORLD
Figure 1.
Mud volcanism is the most developed in Eastern Azerbaijan 
where 30% of all the world’s mud volcanoes are concentrated 
(figure 2). Currently over 300 onshore and offshore mud volcanoes 
are found here. 220 volcanoes out them are concentrated on the area 
of 16,000 km . Many mud volcanoes here are quite large.
For this reason it is no wonder that Azerbaijan is called a 
motherland and country of mud volcanoes - these nature's 
phenomena. Here volcanoes are represented in all their variety and 
magnificence; all types of mud volcanism are found here (active, 
dormant, buried, underwater, island, oil producing). There is no area 
in the world like Azerbaijan in terms of the number of mud
W HAT DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 87
volcanoes, their morphological diversity and activity. In Gobustan 
there is even a unique volcano Goturdag where eruption or mud 
squeezing never interrupts.

Figure 2. Мар o f mud volcanoes o f Azerbaijan
Other regions of wide development of mud volcanism include: 
Russia, Italy, Indonesia, Turkmenistan, Trinidad and Tobago, 
Romania, the Ukraine, Burma, Panama and Japan where the number 
of mud volcanoes ranges from 35 to 60. This group of countries is 
followed by Pakistan, Columbia, Morocco, Iran, China, the USA, 
New Zealand, Venezuela, Nigeria, India and Greece where number 
of volcanoes ranges from 10 to 30.
The analysis of geographic distribution of geological and 
tectonic conditions of mud volcanoes development shows that 
although volcanoes are scattered all over the world they are mainly 
confined to the Alpine-Himalayan and Pacific mobile belts, i.e. they 
are located in the zones that are characterized by intensive modem 
movements of the Earth's emst within historically observable time
88 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
period.
However, volcanoes are not developed everywhere within the 
boundaries of mobile belts. Namely, there are over 170 oil and gas 
bearing and prospective basins within the mobile belts, but mud 
volcanoes are found only in 25 of them, although anticline 
structures, faults, plastic clay sequences, gas accumulation, 
formation water, abnormally high formation pressures that 
according to researchers facilitate development of mud volcanoes 
are found almost in all basins. Based on that it is possible to 
conclude that the above factors are not sufficient for formation of 
mud volcanoes.
Deeper studies result in certain mainly quantitative corrections 
of the range of factors required for formation of mud volcanoes.
Assuming that the majority of mud volcanoes are concentrated 
in the eastern part of Azerbaijan the analysis of geological structure 
and history of development of this area can provide some 
understanding about conditions required for development of mud 
volcanoes.
It is necessary to note that such wide development of mud 
volcanism in Eastern Azerbaijan that tectonically belongs to the 
South-Caspian Depression is not occasional because both the 
history of development and modem geological structure and 
geodynamic condition of this depression are unique even with 
regards to the mobile belts. It is mainly manifested by high speeds 
of downwarping and avalanche sedimentation (up to 3000 m/mln. 
years, with several hundreds of meters in min. years in depressions 
of the Alpine belt with similar geological history of development), 
abnormally low thermal streams (25-50 mW/m with 41-109 
mW/m2 in other depressions of the Alpine belt). These key factors 
result in accumulation of very thick (over 25 km) sedimentary 
sequence within geologically very short time where clay formations 
account for up to 90% of the section. This clay has undercompacted 
character preserving plastic properties and at shallow depths. The 
South-Caspian basin is also characterized by wide development of 
abnormally high formation (pore) pressures (average abnormality
W H A T DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 89
coefficient is 1.8), unsually stretched vertical zonation of 
hydrocarbon generation that covers the interval from the first 
kilometers to 12 and more km and by engagement of a very thick 
sequence of sedimentary rock in the zone of intensive gas 
generation and the most important factor for development of the 
mud volcanism is that this gas generation process continues till 
present time. Strong emissions of gas from the depth observed 
during eruptions of mud volcanoes vividly manifest that.
Additionally, it is necessary to note intensive folding, high 
degree of dislocation of rock, wide development of faulting and 
high seismicity observed here.
All of the above factors to a certain degree reveal the mistery of 
this unique phenomenon and give an idea about natural conditions 
required for development and existence of mud volcanoes.
3.2. VOLCANO, WHAT IS YOUR NATIONAL NAME?
Currently the most generally recognized name for the considered 
natural phenomenon is a "mud volcano". If objects with different 
size are considered then the larger one is termed a mud volcano, 
while the smaller one is named as a mud mount, salse, gryphon. A 
mount is small hill with height ranging from 0.5 to 50 m with base 
diameter from 5 to 150 m. Unlike volcanoes it does not produce 
breccia in the erupted material. Salses are underdeveloped semi­
cones filled with silt and producing gas, water and sometimes oil. 
Diameter of funnels is 0.5 -  30 m. Salses with large sizes of craters 
are classified as mud volcanic lakes, like in Turkmenistan (Rozovy 
or Western Porsugeli). Gryphons are mud and gas vents with height 
up to 1-3 m. Gryphons differ from mud mounts not only in 
elevations but also by the complete absence of even small hard rock 
fragment.
In the literature it is possible to find such definitions as a 
“volcanoid” (E.P.Shteber), a “gas volcano" (S.A.Kovalevsky) or a 
"gas and oil volcano" (V.A.Gorin and Z.A.Buniat-Zadeh) as well as 
a "sedimentary volcano" (G.Kugler).
At the same time in different countries local names are used that
90 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
highlight one or the other aspect of the penomenon or features o f a 
certain type of mud volcanoes. For example, such expressive local 
definitions as "mud mountains", "burnt mountains", “peklo” (hell), 
“blevak” (vomit) are found in the descriptions of Kerch-Taman mud 
volcanoes in addition to the above names.“
A well known local name of a mud volcano in Azerbaijan is 
“pilpilya". In addition to echoic “pilpilya” (that reflects squelching 
of gas bubbles in silty mud) such names as "mud lakes", "bozdag" 
(grey mountain) are used by locals to refer to single rarely erupting 
volcanic cones with tops filled by inactive mass of mud lava that 
has whitish color due to salt films. An “akhtirma” (white coat) is 
used to name a group of volcanic centers of bozdag type that flood 
vast areas with mud flows. It is possible to encounter volcano 
names with a suffix “batan” (from “batmag” -  to bog down), like 
for example Lökbatan (i.e. a place where camels bog down). 
Lökbatan volcano is a 86 m high hill with two peaks. Two knolls on 
the top of this volcano resemble humps of a bogged down camel. 
This is how its name was coined (“Lek” -  camel, “batan” -  bogged 
down). The name “kainarja” (boiling place) is applied to gas 
gryphons venting from a liquid medium (mud, water, oil). There are 
other names, such as Keireki (a forge hearth), Odatanbozdag (a 
mountain that throws fire), Airanteken - a mountain that throws a 
kefir-like liquid, etc.
In Georgia mud volcanoes are mainly named as “akhtala”.
In Turkmenistan a “porsugel” (foam lake, lake of scum) is added 
to the series of the above names. It is applied to mud volcano 
openings filled by gassy turbid water usually covered by a mud 
film. The name “patlaukh” is applied to brecia piles on dormant 
volcanoes. Ak-Patlaukh (white knoll), Gek-Patlaukh (blue knoll), 
Gyumyush-Patlaukh (silver knoll). It is possible to encounter such 
names as “peklo” (hell), “puchina” (heave) in the Kerch peninsula.
In Columbia mud volcanoes are named as “volcanitos”, in 
Trinidad and Tobago (Trinidiad island) they are named as “moms”, 
“buffs”, “yards”, in Romania - "glodurs", "fnerbs", "fierbetors", 
"bolboroses", "pyklis", "sereturs", in Malaysia - "tagai", in
W HAT DO W E K N O W  A B O U T M U D  V O LC AN O ES ? 91
Indonesia - "pootoses", in Venezuela - "ervideroses", in India 
(Andaman Islands) they name mud volcanoes as “jalti”.
In Italy in Emilia and Campania regions they use names like 
“salse" and "bollitory". The first name corresponds to gas gryphons 
composed of silt and the latter one corresponds to boiling gryphons. 
In south of Cicily they use name "makaluba" (destroyer) and in the 
north name "salinelli" (salt ground) is used. In Italy also such names 
as "barbogli, barboi, spesso, bombi" are found.
92 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
IV. HOW A MUD VOLCANO IS FORMED? -  
HYPOTHESES AND MODELS
Despite more than a century-old history of studies of mud 
volcanism scientists still continue to argue about the origin of this 
amazing natural phenomenon. Some associate this process only 
with sedimentary sequence, others see the link with deep processes 
occurring in the mantle.
A number of hypotheses or theories about the origin of mud 
volcanoes were developed: from the earliest model of G.V.Abich 
(1863) who linked mud volcanic process with magmatism to later 
models that consider the relation between development of mud 
volcanism and sedimentation diapirism (Brown, 1990) or associate 
the generation and mechanism of development of mud volcanoes 
with the processes that occur in the Cenozoic fill of molasse troughs 
with Paleogene-Miocene sediments playing the key part in the 
section (Aliyev, 1992). The difference of the views of scientists 
with regard to the formation of mud volcanoes is mainly based on 
the sources of hydrocarbon gas that drives the mechanism of 
volcanism.
The main factors that determined development of mud 
volcanism, namely, in Azerbaijan, include the following: presence 
of plastic clay sequences, formation water, accumulation of 
hydrocarbon gas, tectonic faults and generation of deep abnormally 
high formation pressures that exceed hydrostatic pressure in more 
than 2 times. At the same time the first two factors are mainly 
needed for formation of mud volcanic breccia, while the others are 
needed for creation of conditions to push the breccia to the surface.
In general, a relation of the zones of development of mud 
volcanism with the areas of Cenozoic molasse troughs characterized 
by thick layers of sediments of orogenic complexes is established. 
All areas of development of volcanism are characterized by 
maximum thickness of sedimentary sequence. High concentration 
of volcanoes in Azerbaijan is explained primarily by intensive 
downward warping of the Caspian Depression in the Cenozoic age.
W HAT DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 93
Numerous examples of mud volcanic activities in different regions 
of their development, both in Azerbaijan and in other countries, in 
general confirm the above concept.
4.1. IS IT POSSIBLE TO MODEL A MUD VOLCANO?
Significant amount of experimental and actual data accumulated 
to date, mathematical and physical modeling of mud volcanism 
significantly developed previous concepts providing a more 
justified scientific foundation for them.
The earlier hypotheses were based only on the assumption of 
one or the other geological and geochemical processes, later models 
include relatively detailed analysis of the relations of oil and gas 
generation, abnormally high formation pressure, decompression 
expansion of gas and tectonic processes with diapirism and mud 
volcanism. Interrelation of gas with high pressure of fluids caused 
by the imbalance of compaction should be considered as a main 
driver of formation of volcanoes in Azerbaijan.
Modeling of mud volcanoes activity performed by Azerbaijan 
scientists demonstrated that the ignition of gas emissions of 
volcanoes is attributable to the formation of methane-air fire-damp 
gas with a flash point of above 537°C and the scientists also 
calculated the gas balance for onshore and offshore mud volcanoes 
(A.Sh.Babayev).
4.2. MUD AND MAGMATIC VOLCANOES -  RESEMBLANCE
OR RELATIONSHIP?
Massoudi a well known Arabian traveller, geographer and 
historian was one of the first to pay attention to the similarity of 
mud and magmatic volcanism as far back as in the X century 
describing the eruption of one of mud volcanoes in the Caspian Sea.
Actually, a mud volcano and a lava volcano have similar 
structure of eruptive apparatus and character of activity: a truncated 
volcanic cone with a caldera, crater bar broken by diachronous and 
multidirectional flows of liquid products, tongues of the last 
eruptions, etc. However, the cones of mud volcanoes are much
94 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
lower than the cones of lava volcanoes - the height of mud 
volcanoes does not exceed 500 m. However, it is necessary to take 
into account the fact that the material produced by mud volcanoes 
and composes their slopes is mud that is easily washed out and 
destroyed under the impact of external factors.
Mud volcanoes successfully rival with lava volcanoes in terms 
of the magnitude of eruptions and their disastrous consequences. 
For example, a mushroom cloud of the explosion of mud volcano 
Otmanbozdag in January 1922 located near Baku was seen from the 
hundreds of kilometers and its height reached 600 m.
Does this similarity result from their genetic relationship. 
G.Abich, one of the first researchers of mud volcanes of the 
Caucasus, after studying a piece of a mount breccia from mud 
volcanic island Kumani in 1860 established its chemical and 
petrographic identity with trachytic igneous rock and based on that 
he came to the conclusion that volcanic breccias represent a mixture 
of two different components -  on the one hand, magmatic material 
rising from the depth of volcanoes and, on the other hand, material 
of sedimentary rock of the volcano base pushed by the magmatic 
material erupted to the surface. Mud lava or breccia of mud 
volcanoes is composed of the rock that is mixed and strongly 
altered by hydrochemical processes occurring in this volcano 
(photo 15).
Photo 15. Magmatic volcanoes (eruptions)
S.A.Kovalevsky also did not doubt the relation between the 
"real" volcanism and the mud volcanism. He believed that "there is
W HAT DO W E K N O W  A B O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 95
the same relationship between mud volcanism and violcanic 
activities like the relationship between the flame of a hearth and 
boiling of a sauce pan”. In other words the center of the mud 
volcanism and the real volcanism is one underground magmatic 
source. At the same time the supporters of this hypothesis refer first 
of all to the Cicilian salses - makalubes (from Arabian word maklub 
- destroyer) developed on the slopes of volcano Etna. Mud flows 
very often coincide with lava eruptions. The mud which is the 
mixture of water and silt has high temperature. Composition of gas 
is also mainly volcanic. The bigger is the distance from a lava 
volcano the colder is the mud produced from the craters of salses 
and composition of gas becomes more different from the 
composition of "parent" gas of the Etna. Actually, unlike magmatic 
volcanoes the bodies of mud volcanoes are cold. The temperature of 
fluids and mud produced in the calm periods of gryphone-salse 
activity of a volcano usually ranges from 18 to 25°C which is 
evidently uncomparable with the thermal mud flows observed in the 
caldera of lava volcanoes.
96 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Gullyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
V. LIFE OF MUD VOLCANOES - STUDIES AND 
EYEWITNESS ACCOUNTS
The life of mud volcanoes cover a long geological period from 
its formation to buriall and volcanoes are divided into active and 
dormant volcanoes. The active mud volcanoes erupt many times. 
Between eruptions they undergo a passive gryphon and salse stage. 
This ability of mud volcanoes to die out for more or less long period 
after active eruptions and enter gryphon-salse stage with its 
diminishing activity up to complete loss of all life signatures to a 
certain degree is also charasteristic of lava volcanoes. The length of 
such hiatus periods between eruptions is diffferent for different 
volcanoes and can range from 1-5 years to 50-60 and more years.
400 eruptions of 93 volcanoes have been recorded in Eastern 
Azerbaijan from 1810 till present time. The most active volcanoes 
are Lökbatan, Shikhzarli, Keyreiki, Gushchu and island Hare-Zira 
(Bulla) which in the specified period erupted 23, 22, 18, 13 and 13, 
respectively.
In other regions the frequency of mud volcano eruptions is much 
lower. A number of strong eruptions were recorded in the Taman 
and Kerch peninsulas, in Trinidad Island, in Italy (Sicily), in 
Sakhalin, etc.
According to the results of studies the mud volcano 
paleoactivity started in the Early Miocene time. Intensive eruptions 
of mud volcanoes occurred in the Middle Miocene (Chokrak), 
Upper Miocene (Sarmation), Pliocene, Pleistocene and naturally in 
the last two centuries.
Due to the suddenness and short-time it is not always possible to 
observe the eruptions of mud volcanoes that are usually situated far 
from settlements. The accounts of eyewitnesses (residents of towns, 
shepherds, sailors, light keeprs, etc.) provide certain information 
about the eruptions. According to the summary of such observations 
the eruption starts abruptly with an underground roar or thundering 
rattle that is followed with an explosion, eruption of mud volcanic 
breccia and gas. After that combustible gas ignites producing a
W HAT DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 97
pillar of flame that reaches the height of several hundreds of meters 
(100-300 m and more). The gas bums during more or less long time 
lightening the surrounding area (if eruptions occurs at night time) 
over a large distance. Eruption can occur without a gas flash.
The eruptions in islands Gil (Glinyany) and Hare-Zira in the 
Caspian Sea in 1810 are one of the most earliest recorded eruptions.
It is possible to judge about eruptions over the historic period 
based on diachronous mud volcanic covers that have different 
erosional compartition, color and vegetation (photo 16).
Photo 16. Mud volcano Kechaldag. Eruption on October 10, 2000
Most of the active mud volcanoes are located far from 
settlement, busy highways, technical structures or are located in the 
Caspian Sea bed and seemingly they cannot be classified as natural 
phenomena accompanied by severe consequences. However, there 
are known cases when due to a combination of circumstances a 
volcano eruption caused material damage and even killed people.
According to the accounts of local residents this happened 
during the eruption of volcano Bozdag-Gyuzdek in the Absheron
98
Peninsula 20 km to the west from Baku that was characterized by 
suddenness, strength and fluidity. The crater of the volcano was 
usually used by shepherds for overnight stops, because there was a 
lake there that was used as a drinking place for sheep. In the night 
of eruption in 1902 around 2000 sheeps and six shepherds 
gatherered here. Gas explosion was so rapid that not only animals 
but also people did not have chances to save their lives (photo 17).
Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 17. Island volcano in the Caspian Sea
Strong eruption referred to the XV century near Khanagya 
village according to local legends buried the entire village of Old 
Gyady. The river that flows here quite often washes out old 
household articles and coins.
The effects of the eruption of the volcano on Svinoy island 
(Sengi-Mugan) in the Caspian Sea in April 11, 1932, were very 
tragic. The inhabitants of the island were a light-keeper with 
workers, fishermen with families. Gas blowout and its ignitition 
was so suddent that instaneously entire island was enveloped in 
flames that rose up to 100-200 m. In the result residential and
W HAT DO W E K N O W  ABO U T M UD V O LC AN O ES ? 99
service buildings were destroyed, entire family of the light-keeper 
was killed as well members of families of other residents of the 
island, including 5 children from 2 to 7 years old.
In 1930 the eruption of Voskhodovsky mud volcano (in the east 
of the Kerch peninsula) was accompanied by an explosiotn, fire and 
blowout of oil-impregnated mud to a significant height. Strong 
stream of mud (up to 3 m high) flowed towards Djardjavy island 
and buried several one-floor buildings.
100 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
VI. GROWING MOUNTAINS
The speed of geological processes is very slow and geologists 
usually judge about them based on indirect data. Mud volcanoes 
provide a unique opportunity not only to observe geological 
processes but also to quantity them.
The protrusion of broken clay bending upward in a large flat 
tape from a crater hole was observed in many volcanoes. For 
example, the last eruption of Goturdag volcano in Azerbaijan 
occurred in 1987 but it is still possible to observe plasticine-like 
breccia continuously squeezed from the crater like a toothpase from 
a tube. The velocity and amount of squeezed breccia varies with 
time.
The movement of mount mud from the crater along the slope of 
a volcano resembles creeping of a glacial tongue with different 
velocities of the stream in the central part and at the margins.
Calculations made based on results of observations with 
intervals 3.5 and 11 months show that the speed of squeezing is 
rather stable in the middle. It is around 3.5 m per month. One of the 
most unusual mud volcanoes in the north-western Caucasus is 
Raznokolsky volcano that is characterized by squeezing of a 
peculiar mud volcanic dyke with the speed of 2.5 - 8 cm/day. 
Within a year it was nonuniformly squeezed from the Earth’s 
interior by 1.5 - 10 m (photo 18).
As peasants near Kerch say the small volcano located here 
slowly but steadily grows increasing its height wihout the mud 
eruption.
The growth of volcanic cones without eruption of mud to the 
surface is also very common in Azerbaijan. It is easily determined 
here based on the relations of growing structures and young Caspian 
terraces. According to S.A. Kovalevsky the average rate of growth 
of Kyursangi mountain is up to 15 cm/year.
There are multiple cases of injection of tectonic breccia under 
the covers of old mud volcanic breccia and bed rock on volcano 
slopes.
W H A T DO W E K N O W  ABO U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 101
Photo IS. The tongues after an eruption
Such heaving usually occurs during eruptions of volcanoes and 
leads in rapid and sometimes significant rises (up to 10 m) of 
mobile parts of volcanic mountain covering an area of several 
hectares. Namely, during the eruption of island volcano Los 
(Garasu) in 1923 high uplifting of boulders of Upper Pliocene 
formations above the sea level was observed. Before the eruptions 
they were under water. During fire eruption in 1932 in Svinoy 
island a 10 m area of adjacent sea bed in the northern part of the 
island consisting of old mud volcano breccia was lifted up to 10 m 
and the central part of the island lowered. The same happened to 
Byandovan in 1932 - the eruption lifted the sea bed part composed 
of breccia and coupled it with the coast strip.
Strong eruptions of mud also play significant role in forming of 
cones of mud volcanoes. As it was noted the length of some tongue­
like flows of high volcanoes reaches several km. For example, 
south-western flows of Otmanbozdag stretch for 2.5-3 km. The 
width of the flow on the slope of volcano slope is 100-200 m. 
Thickness of flow ranges from 5-6 m to 20 m depending on the
102
density of breccia. All these sizes are mainly determined by the 
significant amount of the mass erupted by a volcano at a time. 
Y.Shegren who was in Baku during Lökbatan eruption in 1887 
inidicates that the eruption volume was 200,000 m3, while the 
amount of mud erupted by relatively smaller Italian mud volcano 
Sassuolo near Modena in 1835 was estimated by engineer Brinioli 
di Brunkof at 1.5 min. m3. The amount of mud erupted by Keireki 
volcano in 1885 according to calculations of N.Barbo de Mami and 
S.Simanovich is approximantely 350,000 m3. The eruption on 
Gorelaya mountain (Taman peninsula) produced around 1 min. m3 
of volcanic products. The eruptions of mud volcanic breccia with 
amount of 1 min. m3 and more were also observed in mud 
volcanoes of Azerbaijan, namely, Dashmardan (2 min. m3) in 1924, 
Chapylmysh (2.5 min. m3) in 1939, Garasu island (1 min. m3) in 
1977, Sengi-Mugan island (3.5 min. m3) in 2002, etc. Very large 
eruptions were recorded in the XIX century, for example again in 
Dashmardan in 1866 (7.4 min. m3) and Otmanbozdag volcano in 
1854 (20 min. m3).
The results of exploration of Azerbaijan mud volcanoes are 
quite interesting. It was conducted by drilling a number of wells in 
the breccia cover for measurement of the thickness of eruption 
mantle, studying of undermount relief and bedding in the covered 
bedrock and evaluation of the magnitude and character of eruptive 
channel of the volcano. 22 volcanoes were studied and it was 
established that the thickness of breccia caps in different volcanoes 
ranges from 40 to 110 m.
The volume of mud volcanic breccia erupted by mud volcanoes 
of Azerbaijan is estimated at over 120 min. m3.
Comparison of the amount of mud volcanic material produced 
during one eruption and its total volume allows provides some idea 
about paleoactivity of volcanoes. For instance, 30,000 nr of 
volcanic breccia was produced during eruption of mud volcano 
Touragai in 1947 and total amount is 343. 106 nr3. Therefore, over 
5000 eruptions were needed to form Touragai volcano assuming 
that every eruption produces approximately the same amount of
Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev W H AT DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M U D  V O LC AN O ES ? 103
breccia. The total volume o f breccia Kyanizadag is 735 106 m3, 
while the last eruption produced 350,000 nr of breccia. Proceeding 
from these considerations over 7000 eruptions are needed to form 
Kyanizadag volcano. 2 min. m3 o f breccia was produced during 
eruption o f Dashmardan volcano in 1954, total amount o f breccia is 
2500 10 m3. Here, apparently, 1200 eruptions occurred. Using the 
same calculations it was found that 650 eruptions were needed to 
form mud volcano Keireki, 550 eruptions were needed to form 
Dashgil volcano, etc.
6.1. AWAKENING AFTER SLUMBER
There are too many mud volcanoes in Azerbaijan and from 3 to 
5 eruptions occur here every year. There are periods of noticeable 
activation o f volcanoes when the number o f eruptions increases. 
Namely, during the last century in 1926, 1970, 1977, 1986, 1988 
there were from six to nine o f recorded eruptions o f mud volcanoes. 
The record o f 16 eruptions o f onshore and offshore volcanoes was 
observed in the beginning of new millenium in 2001. After a short 
calm period in 2004 again 7 eruptions o f  volcanoes were recorded 
in the country (figure 3).
Figure 3. The intensity o f  mud volcanoes eruptions in Azerbaijan. 
A- one time, В up to 5 lime, C from 5 to 10 times, D more than 10 times
104 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Unexpected eruption of a volcano is an amazing spectacle that 
sometimes frightens people who stay nearby. Eruptions shake 
ground, produce large amounts of volcanic brecca forming pillars of 
fire with combustion temperature of 1000-12000. Breccia produced 
by the volcano flows down along slopes forming whimsical 
eruption tongues (photo 19).
Photo 19. Eruption ofDashmardan volcano (May 12, 2011)
The eruptions of sea volcanoes are even more notable. On the 
one hand, it is spectacular and impressive water fountain in the sea 
that gradually turns into a pillar of flame amid the blue of the sea, 
on the other hand it accompanied by a sudden emergence of an 
island amid the sea just in front of your eyes that can be more than 5 
m high. But such islands usually do not exist for a long time. The 
Caspian waves wash them out turning them into underwater banks. 
A vivid example is the eruption of the volcano of Makarova bank 
(Bakhar-deniz) in 1958. In the evening an island was formed after 
the eruption, by it was washed out by the next morning. Same 
phenomena happened with volcano B.Pilpilya - in Buzovny in 1953
W HAT DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M U D  V O LC AN O ES ? 105
and in 2001 the eruption of this sea volcano formed an island that 
existed only for ten days (photo 20). There are such islands that 
exist for a long time. For example, a bank Pogorelaya Plita (Yanan 
Tava) in the Baku Archipelago considered to be an island during 40
year.
Photo 20. Island remnant after the eruption o f March 21, 2001
There is one more form of volcano eruption. This is an eruption 
without production of mud when mud volcanic breccia is squeezed 
from the vent of a volcano. This is a rather rare phenomenon. Only 
two volcanoes in Azerbaijan, Cheildag and Goturdag, were formed 
by such mud flow.
The eruption of Cheildag that started on June 4, 1970, continued 
for almost a months, however, with some slowing of the squeezing 
process. Semi-dry mud volcanic breccia here formed a 50 x 60 m 
dome that is up to 4 m high. In the first days the speed of movement 
of this mass was over 1 m per day. It is significant, that during all 
this time (3 months) the burning of hydrocarbon gas coming from
cracks continued. The last eruption of this volcano occurred in 2004 
(photo 21).
106____________________________ Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 21. Volcano Che i ldag. Breccia squeezing process
The continuous eruption (mud squeezing) of Gouturdag volcano 
lasted for over 100 year. Semi-dry breccia was squeezed from 50 m 
long and 15 m wide crater hole forming a ribbon that steeply heaved 
and then broke creeping down along the slop of the volcano 
(photo 22). The velocity of the flow in 1926-1927 was 42 m per 
year. Same squeezing process occurs in Jiginsk volcano in Western 
Kuban.
It is necessary to say that each volcano eruption is a new piece 
of information about processes occurring in the Earth's interior 
which allows to understand the essence of this process more deeply 
and possibly to predict future eruptions. And of the reasons of the 
awakening of volcanoes is a technogenic factor - unreasonable 
economic activities of people.
W H A T DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 107
Photo 22. Volcano Goturdag. Slow process o f mud squeezing
6.2. DO NOT DISTURB A DORMANT VOLCANO
It can have tragic effects. In October 2000 this happened with 
Kelchadag that is situated in the south-eastern coast of Jeiranbatan 
reservoir in Azerbaijan. Operations performed on the slopes of this 
long-dormant volcano, evidently, triggered its awakening and an 
enormous eruption occurred. The breccia erupted from the volcano 
buried unfinished houses. Fortunately, there were no victims (photo 
23, 24).
A huge pit was excavated in summer 2001 near the crater of 
Lökbatan volcano that is the most active volcano in Azerbaijan 
(Photo 23). Thoughtless economic activities triggered awakening of 
this volcano in October of the same year. It should be always kept 
in mind: do not disturb a dormant volcano, it can results in bad 
consequences.
In most of the cases technogenic processes have a serious impact 
on acitivization of volcanism. We witnessed this phenomenon in 
1974 when we worked in the Crimea.
108 Ad. A. Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 24. An excavation near the crater triggering a volcano eruption
Not far from Kerch at the outskirts of Soldatskaya Sloboda 
village the workers who carried out construction of a pipeline had to 
excavate the second trench because the the first one near a mud 
volcano was filled by breccia and was deformed. The example of
Photo 23. Volcanic breccias covers buildings after the eruption
W H AT DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC AN O ES ? 109
construction of water supply system of Novoselovka village is even 
more illustrative. Here a construction of a water catchment basin 
was started at the outskirts of a village on a small hill near a long­
time dormant mud volcano. After a pit was excavated that was 
around 20 in long, 9 m wide and 2.5 m deep an eruption of volcanic 
mud started that filled the entire pit. A dormant volcano should not 
be used for any type of structures: roads, different pipelines.
6.3. EARTHQUAKES AND MUD VOLCANOES
The energy is accumulating and periodically releasing in the 
Earth’s interior since the formation and development of the planet. 
Maximum manifestations of the discharge of accumulated energy 
are earthquakes, eruptions of lava and mud volcanoes. For this 
reason there should be a relation (mutual sequence) between these 
natural phenomena and such relation is currently established.
Photo 25. Mount broken during the volcano eruption
Namely, a statistical analysis of distribution of earthquakes and 
eruptions of mud volcanoes in Azerbaijan by months in the period 
since 1810 till the current time showed that seismic activization 
results in eruptions of mud volcanoes and in most of the cases
110
earthquakes occur before mud volcano eruptions. The latter is 
explained by the fact that the energy of earthquakes significantly 
exceeds the energy of eruptions of mud volcanoes being the 
determining factor of the underground energy discharge (photo25).
So underground shock triggers an earthquake. Many years of 
observations of mud volcanoes activities in Azerbaijan, comparative 
analysis of earthquake and eruption data over the last two centuries 
convinced volcanologists that there is a genetic relationship 
between activities of mud volcanoes and seismicity. In the 80s of 
the last century we conducted monitoring on some volcanoes of the 
Absheron peninsula, Gobustan and Shamakha district. The results 
of observations showed that at the last stage of "preparation" for an 
earthquake the volcanoes become more active than before and 
concentrations of some components such as CO2, nitrogen, helium, 
boron, chloride in produced gas and water reaches anomalous 
levels, i.e. gas and hydrogeochemical signatures of activization of 
mud volcanic activities as possible earthquake precursors were 
identified (photo 26).
Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 26. Activation o f a volcano is a precursor o f an eruption
W HAT DO W E K N O W  AB O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 111
Figure 4. Relationship o f mud volcano eruptions with earthquakes
It was established that earthquakes play a role of a triggering 
mechanism in mud volcanic process. This causal relation is 
observed when an earthquake epicenter (source) and volcano are 
situated within the boundaries of one fault structure and if mud 
volcano was dormant for a prolonged period and accumulated 
sufficient energy for eruption. For example, in 1902 strong eruption 
of Shikhzarli in Marazy area started 15 minutes after a disastrous 
earthquake in Shemakha. In 1927 the eruption of Jau-tepe volcano 
on the Kerch peninsula occurred at the same time with the Crimean 
earthquake. There are a lot of similar examples. A record number of 
earthquakes (16) occurred in the new millennium in 2001 after 
strong Caspian earthquakes with magnitude of 6-7 that occurred on 
November 25 and December 6, 2000.
112
Seismic activation of the Earth’s interior charges one kind of 
volcanoes with energy due to activation of regional faults, 
dislocations, fractures and intensification of gas inflow into the 
eruptive apparatus and it triggers eruptions of other volcanoes being 
in critically metastable state. The example of the latter case are 
eruptions of two large mud volcanoes (Shikhzarli and Bozdag- 
Gyuzdek) that are situated on the extension of the axis of 
catastrophic earthquake that occurred in the Shemakha on January 
13, 1902 (figure 4).
The above sensitivity of mud volcanoes to seismic shocks was 
repeatedly observed in Azerbaijan and in the other regions of their 
development, for example, in Turkmenistan, Sakhalin Island, in 
Italy, etc.
Thus earthquake trigger eruptions of mud volcanoes and at the 
same time eruptions of mud volcanoes lead to local shaking of 
surrounding areas, i.e. volcanic earthquake. The energy class of 
shaking (K) that was for the first time defined by A.A.Yakubov,
F.T. Kuliyev and T.A. Ismail-Zadeh during the Lökbatan mud 
volcano eruption on October 1, 1972 was in average equal to 8.9 
which corresponds to the energy of weak earthquakes.
Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev W HAT DO W E K N O W  ABO U T M UD VO LC AN O ES ? 113
VII. BREATH OF MUD VOLCANOES
Ther large number attempts of experimental and theoretical 
estimations of the volumes of mud volcanoes activities products 
(gas, breccia, water) that were brought to the Earth’s surface are 
known up to date.
The gases produced by mud volcanoes are one of the main 
factors of their origin and for this reason quantitative estimations of 
gas emissions can help to understand the driving force of this 
peculiar natural element.
According to the measurements carried out on dozens of mud 
volcanoes of Azerbaijan gas flow rates in the dormant periods vary 
in a wide range. For example, gas flow rate in the silty crater of a 
large salse of Dashgil volcano reached 40,000 m3 per day. When the 
measurement was repeated after 13 months this flow rate reached 
8,000 m3 and after 12 months it dropped to 200 m3, after another 12 
months it dropped to 200 m3. Then the volcano gas activity again 
intensified. According to these numbers the average daily gas 
discharge rate of Dashgil volcano is around 20,000 m3.
Measurements made by F.G.Dadashev on 242 vents of 21 
volcanoes showed that in dormant periods gas discharge rates of 
different volcanoes range from 0,1 mVyear to 731 m3/year.
Total annual amount of gas produced by all volcanoes of 
Azerbaijan is around 20 mln.m3 /year.
Certain amount of gas (approximately 2cm3 per kg of rock) is 
discharged as a result of degassing of volcanic breccia.
However, most of the gas is produced during paroxysm of 
eruptions of volcanoes. According to existing estimations based on 
the duration of burning and height of the flame eruptions produce 
hundreds of millions of m3 of gas. 30 min. nr3 of gas was discharged 
during the eruption of Lökbatan mud volcano in 1977, 65 min. m3 
of gas was discharged during the eruption of mud volcano Duvanny 
(Zenbil). Shikhzarli emitted even greater amount of gas in 1902.
As it was noted around 400 eruptions of 93 volcanoes were 
recorded in Azerbaijan from 1810 till present time. It is estimated
114 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
that the annual amount of gas produced during eruptions by all 
volcanoes of Azerbaijan is around 250 min. m3 and total amount of 
gas produced during Quaternary period is 175x10 bcm.
The flow rates of water produced by mud volcanoes are 
insignificant and range from 0.01 to 12 mVday. Volcanoes of Alat 
range are water rich. The largest among them are Bakhar, Dashgil, 
Airanteken, Solakhai. These volcanoes in total carried out around 
20 mVday of water to surface. According to the measurements made 
on 53 volcanoes of Azerbaijan the total water flow rate is around 73 
mVday. Extrapolating this value to all active volcanoes of 
Azerbaijan (excluding offshore volcanoes) it is possible to calculate 
that approximate total water production rate is 200 mVday or 730 
bcm/year.
Significant amount of water is produced by volcanoes during 
eruptions with breccia. It was calculated that the amount of water 
produced by volcanoes of Azerbaijan during their eruptions is 
around 24 km3.
Special observations revealed the impact of mud volcanoes on 
subsoil geotemperature conditions. Eruptive apparatus of mud 
volcanoes is a peculiar kind of channel where the heat is transferred 
from the depth to the surface more intensively which is manifested 
by the association of temperature anomalies with parts of structures 
that are affected by mud volcanoes. The area of mud volcano 
development is marked by an increased thermal flux.
In 1924 professor S. A.Kovalevsky during a geological excursion 
made an interesting description of the temperature regime of 
Lokabatan which is the most active mud volcano of Azerbaijan: 
“Bluish smoke of hot gas seeps is catched in the crater hollow. The 
bottom and walls of the crater near hot gas streams have purple 
grey, pale pink and red shades of breccia clay burning (Photo ). The 
surface of breccia at the crater bottom is broken by cracks through 
which hot gas and water vapor breaks. Rock temperature on the 
crater is such that it is possible bum one’s feet through soles when 
walking and it was necessary to cool down for half an hour rock 
fragments broken from boulders exposed to hot streams to be able
W HAT DO W E K N O W  A B O U T M U D  V O LC A N O E S ? 115
to hold them by hand without burning oneself' (observations were 
made after an eruption).
During the second excursion 2 years later, the volcano was still 
hot apparently after an eruption, though it was not so hot like it was 
during the first trip. Rock temperature near the surface in the hottest 
spot this time was only 130° C.
There are very few observations of the temperatures of gas 
produced from strong gryphons after eruptions. The gas stream 
temperature measured by D.V. Golubyatnikov after one of mud 
volcano emption 50°C. Approximately the same temperature was 
recorded five days after the emption of Otmanbozdag volcano 
(Azerbaijan). Liquid mud in the crater of Touragai volcano six days 
after its eruption had comparable temperature (43°C).
Temperature of produced liquid emissions on Keimir volcano 
(Turkmenistan) measured in the crater was 43°C while the 
temperature of water in surrounding lakes of the secondary craters 
was only 27°C.
Thus, positive temperature anomalies within the mud volcano 
area are dependent on movement of thermal fluids along their 
eruptive channels.
116 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
VIII. MUD VOLCANOES IN THE SPACE EMBRACE
8.1. THE MOON and SUN TRIGGER VOLCANOES
An unusual article in one scientific magazine drew attention of 
all volcanologists of the Globe. Volcanologist V.A. Peret after 
calculating mutual position of the Moon, Sun and Earth for the 
near-term period predicted sharp activation of the Etna on July 27. 
Specialists were skeptical about this news because according to the 
data of direct monitoring of the volcano crater its activity was 
declining. However, the seemingly dormant volcano roared and 
black cloud covered its peak on July 27 when the maximum lunar 
and solar tide was observed. Since that period scientists have started 
to trace and identify regularities and relationships between volcanic 
activities and space processes.
Photo 27. Impact o f  the solar eclipse on the activation o f a mud volcano
According to the current concepts mud volcanoes with small 
mud and gas apparatus are the most sensitive to the changes in the
W HAT DO W E K N O W  ABO U T M UD V O LC AN O ES ? 117
environment and for this reason they provide good opportunities for 
revealing the relations of the Earth's interior with the space. Special 
studies that have been conducted during recent years confirm this 
concept to a certain degree.
Currently, the most well-grounded and rather reliable is the 
impact of lunar and solar tidal effects on mud volcanoes. 
Gravitational impact on the Earth that becomes the most perceptible 
when the Moon is in its perigee the point of the moon’s orbit at 
which it is nearest the Earth or in the same line with the Sun and the 
Earth (during the solar and lunar eclipses) that influences its 
rotation and causes fluctuation of the surface layers quite often 
serves as an additional force that determines discharge of the 
internal energy accumulated in the center of a volcano.
In 1955 Azeri scientists on studying 150-year statistics of the 
eruptions of the Caucasian mud volcanoes and astronomic tables of 
mutual position of the Moon, Earth and Sun in the same period 
established that approximately 60% of all eruptions (there were 200 
eruptions) occurred in the new moon and full moon periods. The 
forecast of mud volcanoes activity in the next four years was made 
based on this forecast. This forecast was completely confirmed: 
nine major eruptions occurred in 1957-1960 completely matched 
predicted timelines.
During total solar eclipse on July 31, 1981, that was observed 
over significant part of the Euro-Asian continent special 
observations on mud volcanoes of Azerbaijan and Turkmenistan 
recorded their significant activization. Gas flow rates increases, 
some dormant mounts were broken, new gas microvents were 
formed.
Attempts were taken to explain the increase in volcanic activity 
by the impact of the Sun in line with the words of the well-known 
English astronomer S.Mitton that "the Sun is a celestial body that 
has the greatest impact on the Earth". As a result it was concluded 
that the periods of the solar activity increase correspond to the 
periods of increase of mud volcano activity all over the world and 
the existence of a confident relationship of mud volcano Akhtala
118
(Georgia) both with the magnitude of the solar activity and its 
fluctuation in time was justified based on the special observations of 
the activity of this volcano.
The solar eclipse impact on the activity of mud volcano was 
observed on Bakhar volcano (Azerbaijan) situated in the area 
Caspian Sea coastal area. During the eclipse the activity of the salse 
on the slope was strongly increased and in front of our very e>es it 
was quickly filled with water releasing gas (photo 27).
Scientific and technical progress in the second half of our 
century provided an opportunity to study the Earth's structure from 
the deep space. For this reason today we have a true notion of bow 
mud volcanoes look like from the space. In accordance with tiese 
studies not only mud volcanoes but also dynamics of their act vity 
is clearly defined (observed).
8.2. SEARCHING FOR THE BREATHING RHYTHMS 
OF VOLCANOES
Rhythmicity is one of the most distinct and common features of 
natural systems. It is observed almost in all processes related to the 
organic and inorganic nature. Light, sound, sea waves, ocean tides, 
alternation of day and night, alternation of seasons, cyclic character 
of geological processes, rhythms of the solar activity, etc. - these are 
different forms of oscillating movements. On a level with the 
shortest oscillations with periods of thousandths and millionths of 
seconds found in the physics of the microcosm there are oscillations 
with periods that cover a very wide range: seconds, minutes, hours, 
days, seasons, years and centuries. Global cyclic phenomena with 
repetition frequency of thousands, millions and even billions of 
years are found only in geological objects.
Experimental observations and Fourier decomposition of 
accumulated data showed that mud volcanoes are also familiar with 
rhythms.
It was found that variations in gas discharge rate of Dashgil 
volcano (Azerbaijan) are associated with alternation of day and 
night. At night discharge rates increased and in day time discharge
Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev W HAT DO WE K N O W  A B O U T MUD V O LC A N O E S ? 119
decreased.
Laser measurements over the methane vent of mud volcano 
Gyzmeidan (Azerbaijan) revealed high-frequency oscillations with 
the period from several minutes to dozens of minutes.
The established mutual relation between the space and the Earth 
is also manifested by the fact that rhythms characterizing different 
space objects are found in many natural phenomena, namely, in the 
activity of mud volcanoes. Rhythmically changing radiation of the 
Sun with the period of around 11 years has the strongest impact on 
the Earth among all rhythmical impacts of the space on the Earth.
The variation of the activity of around 300 volcanoes of the 
world was analyzed in the search for such periodicity in the activity 
of mud volcanoes. As a result 9-12 year cycles of mud volcanic 
activity were found. They mainly coincide with 11-year cycles of 
the solar activity.
11-year periodicity is found in mudflow fluctuations of Akhtala 
volcano (Georgia). Retrospective analysis of Azerbaijan mud 
volcanoes data found the rhythms of their activity not only in time 
but also in space. It is found that there is an alternation of the cycles 
of volcano activity from the north-west to south-east and back.
120 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
IX. MUD VOLCANO AS AN INDICATOR OF THE 
BOWELS OIL AND GAS PRESENCE
Currently almost all geologists of the world acknowledge that 
mud volcanoes (i.e. volcanoes that produce hydrocarbon gas) are 
direct surface signatures of the presence of subsurface oil and gas in 
the areas where these volcanoes are developed. However, for a long 
time some specialist referred the areas “affected” by mud volcanoes 
to commercially non-attractive because they believed that mud 
volcanoes destroy subsurface accumulations of oil and gas (figure 5).
Figure 5. Lökbatan mud volcano. Geological section
At the same time some geologists had an opposite view, i.e. they 
believed that volcanoes on the contrary help for accumulation of oil 
deposits. There were even those who called for drilling oil in 
volcanoes.
The prolonged discussion of this issue was finished in 1933 
when a strong gush of oil with the rate of up to 20,000 tons blew 
from well No.45 drilled on Lökbatan volcano on the Absheron 
peninsula and it was proved that oil deposit is not destroyed in the
W HAT DO W E K N O W  A B O U T M U D  V O LC A N O E S ? 121
mud volcano zone. Thus, in these years the genetic relationship of 
the mud volcanism with oil field was for the first time confirmed on 
the example of Lökbatan volcano and it became clear that it was 
necessary to search for new fields near volcanoes.
It is necessary to note that around 28 min. tons of oil and 1 bcm3 
of natural gas was produced over 80 years of development of 
Lökbatan field. An famous well No.45 is still running producing oil 
from this field though with a rate of several tons per day (photo 28).
Photo 28. Borehole No. 45
122 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
In Azerbaijan and in adjacent Turkmenistan many large and rich 
oil, gas and gas condensate fields are associated with mud volcanic 
structures.
It is necessary to note that the relation of mud volcanoes with oil 
and gas deposits was indicated at the earliest days of the study of 
this most interesting natural phenomena. In 1932 
N.I.Voskoboinikov and A.V.Guiyev wrote that mud eruptions are 
caused by hydrocarbon gas that is produced by oil fields. We can 
read the following in the journey notes of N.I.Palibin (1875): "Mud 
volcano Bogboga (it is on the Absheron Peninsula) is an 
underground laboratory where oil is thrown".
Affirming that there is a relationship between mud volcanoes 
and presence of oil and gas it is necessary to note that this 
relationship is not simple. Mud volcano is not a natural well drilled 
by the nature in an oil and gas field. Both mud volcanoes and fields 
belong to different stages of a single oil and gas generation process 
that has distinctive vertical zonation. According to this zonation that 
was firstly developed by N.B.Vassoevich in 1948 based on the 
sedimentary and migration (biogenic) genesis of hydrocarbons in 
the upper layers of the Earth firstly only gas is generated 
(hydrocarbons primarily produce methane) and then as rock 
submerges a zone of intensive generation of oil and wet gas 
(methane homologue) is found and this oil generation zone deeper 
is replaced by the zone of intensive gas generation (methane 
generation).
Thus, the lower zone of intensive gas generation is the source o f 
hydrocarbon gas of mud volcanoes that mainly consist of methane 
(85-100%). Observations on Lökbatan oil field provide a very vivid 
confirmation of the above concept. It was noted that an intensive 
development of this field does not affect the activity of the mud 
volcano. Frequent eruptions of Lökbatan volcano have almost no 
impact on the flow rates of surrounding wells.
Thus, this very large oil field with tremendous gas pressure that 
produced at the early stage of development up to 20,000 tons of oil 
per day from the upper horizons (depth of around 2 km) turned out
W HAT DO WE K N O W  A B O U T  MUD V O LC A N O E S ? 123
to be almost completely sealed in the Earth's interior even with the 
presence of a volcano vent and its intensive activity. At the same 
time the methane occurring much deeper (8-10 km) below the zone 
of intensive gas generation is uncontainable and regularly breaks 
out by strong eruptions.
Thus the association of mud volcanoes with oil and gas fields is 
in the fact that hydrocarbons of both volcanoes and fields are 
produced by the same process of oil and gas generation in the 
sedimentary sequence and it is clearly confirmed by the presence of 
commercial oil and gas in the structures affected by mud volcanoes.
X. VENTS OF SUBSEA VOLCANOES ARE GAS 
HYDRATE SYNTHESIS LABORATORIES
The State Committee on Inventions and Discoveries of the 
USSR on March 19, 1969, registered a scientific discoveiy of a 
previously unknown property of natural gas to form deposits in the 
solid gas hydrate state under certain thermodynamic conditions, 
Formation and accumulation of gas hydrates in the onshore deposits 
was associated with the upper part of sedimentary cover in the 
permafrost zones (under below zero temperatures). Gas hydrates 
can also be formed in the World Ocean under low temperature and 
high pressure conditions. The modern thermodynamic conditions of 
the sedimentary cover of the Earth's crust in the 25% of land and 
around 90% of the World Ocean area are believed to correspond to 
the conditions of accumulation and retention of natural gas in the 
solid hydrate state.
The Caspian Sea also has favorable thermodynamic conditions 
for hydrate formation. At the same time an important factor of 
formation of of hydrocarbon hydrate accumulations is a wide 
development of mud volcanoes in the Southern Caspian Sea that 
supply huge amounts of hydrocarbon gas. In this respect it was 
suggested that the vents of some mud volcanoes could be a very 
good place for formation of gas hydrates. Special surveys conducted 
in the late 70s of the last century confirmed this hypothesis. The 
first gas hydrates were found in the mud volcanic breccias of one
volcano. More intensive studies in 1986-1988 discovered here 
hydrate formation zones on Vezirov uplift (Shatsky Rise) and 
Azizbekov uplift and found convincing signatures of presence of 
gas hydrates in the one of the uplifts of Abich Rise. During these 
years for the first time in the world gas hydrates were mapped in the 
vents of the volcanoes named Bozdag, Elm and Abich. Later more 
than 10 gas hydrate occurrence were found in the Caspian shelf of 
Azerbaijan and it became evident that the Caspian Sea is a large 
world-class gas hydrate province. Gas hydrates has a methane 
composition (62-76%), concentration of the sum of methane 
homologues ranged from 21 to 28%, concentration of CO2 was 1.2- 
7.9%, low concentrations of nitrogen, hydrogen sulfide, hydrogen 
and helium were also found. In terms of the isotopic composition of 
the methane carbon the gas of gas hydrates is identical with the gas 
of oil and gas fields of this area.
Larges gas hydrate reserves were found in the Black Sea. 
Currently, Japanese, Canadian, American, Russian, Norwegian and 
Indian scientist try to develop the technology for commercial 
production of gas from the offshore gas hydrate deposits.
124____________________________ Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev W HAT DO W E KN O W  A B O U T M U D  V O LC A N O E S ? 125
XI. MUD VOLCANOES ARE SOURCES OF 
VALUABLE RESOURCES
11.1. MUD VOLCANOES PRODUCE MINERALS
The world of minerals associated with the mud volcanism is 
amazingly diverse. Currently, over one hundred of minerals have 
been described. Most of them are inherited from the rock altered 
and produced by mud volcanoes. A small group of mineral types 
genetically related with mud volcanism processes presents a special 
interest. The minerals of mud volcanic origin reflect complex 
multistage physical and chemical processes of interaction of 
volcanic water and gas with host lithological sequences broken by 
mud volcanoes.
The most common mineral is pyrite that is especially 
characteristic of Azerbaijan, Kerch-Taman volcanoes. 
Accumulations of fresh sulfur pyrite, crystalline pyrite crusts on 
different rock fragments of volcanic breccias separate well-formed 
crystals disseminated in clay of mound sludge are very common in 
the mud erupted by these volcanoes. The largest pyrite crystals (up 
to 10 cm in the face) were found in the fresh volcanic deposits on 
mud volcano Shikhzarli in Gobustan (photo 29).
Minerals with mud volcanic origin also include: native graphite; 
sulfides - cinnabar, sphalerite, wurtzite, molibdenite, galena, 
realgar, auripigment; sulphosalts -  dufrenoysite; oxides - red copper 
ore; carbonates -  malachite; sulphates - barite, hexanhydrite; 
borates - luneburgite, boronatrocalcite, etc; haloids - fluorite; 
phosphates -  apatite, dernite, complex iron phosphate, magnesium 
phosphate, calcium phosphate.
Minerals produced as a result of mud volcanic activity are 
characterized by absence of rounding, tender and fine forms, they 
are often are represented by fragile separate crystalline assemblages.
The similarity of the association of minerals of mud volcanic 
origin with the association of minerals characteristic of low 
temperature hydrothermal processes draws an attention.
126 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 29. Pyrite crystals produced by mud volcanoes
11.2. MUD VOLCANIC BRECCIA IS A VALUABLE 
NONMETALLIC MINERAL RESOURCE
Mud volcanoes are not only associated with of oil and gas and 
help geologists to explore and discover subsurface deposits of oil 
and gas. A mud volcano like a super-deep well provides 
information about processes occurring in the Earth's interior. 
Volcanic mud contains many valuable microelements such as 
borate, manganese, lithium, vanadium, copper, etc. Volcanic water 
is rich in organic substances, borate, bromine, iodine.
Volcanic clay can be used as a high quality raw material for 
production of cement, keramzite, brick, metallurgical pellets and for 
this it is widely used in the construction. Volcanic breccia is an 
eruption product that contains a range of valuable chemical 
elements, metals that can be extracted and used for economic needs 
(photo 30).
W HAT DO WE K N O W  A B O U T  M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 127
Photo 30. Oil-bearing sandstone and oil shale in volcanic breccia
Given wide occurrence of volcanic breccia in the Kerch 
peninsula, its significant thickness, good geological and technical 
parameters, short distances from manufacturing factories and 
customers it made possible to expect that this region has high 
potential as a resource base for keramzite production.
Preliminary tests of breccias of several mud volcanoes showed 
that they can be used as additives for production of metallurgical 
pellets instead of bentonite clay.
Dolomitized limestone, sand and clay composing mud 
volcanoes are commonly used in the road and building construction. 
For example, the quarry in the area of Voskhodovsky mud volcano 
in the Kerch peninsula is known for many years.
Not long ago Azerbaijan geologists paid attention to active 
binding properties of solid products of mud volcano activities that 
are determined by high dispersity of minerals composing volcanic 
mud, presence of amorphous silica (glass) and lime (CaO). These 
properties of the mud allow to produce construction materials such 
as bricks, including unfired bricks, with a simplified technology and 
low power costs.
Accumulations of secondary iron oxides with bright yellow, 
crimson, orange, red shades are formed on the surface of 
argillaceous siderite and along the cracks in the result of oxidation 
of argillaceous siderite. This ochre can be used as a raw material for 
production of mineral paints. Accumulations of loose bright yellow
colored secondary iron sulphate - jarosite -  can also be used for this 
purpose.
Recently, volcanic clay has been widely used by households as a 
cleaning abrasive material.
11.3. VOLCANIC MUD IS A NATURAL MEDICATION
Mud preparations produced mainly from silt, peat and sapropelic 
muds are widely used for medical purposes in the form of 
injections, baths.
Volcanic mud has also a wide medical application as a valuable 
therapeutic agent. This mud is enriched with mineral salts, organic 
substances, microelements and has healing properties with 
beneficial impact on the human health. It is used in many countries 
where there are mud volcanoes. This mud has been used in Italy 
since the XV century. In the Taman peninsula they started to use in 
the middle of the XIX century. In the former USSR period there 
was an all-Soviet resort Akhtala in Georgia. Volcanic mud as a raw 
material for mud therapy is applied outside resorts in the clinics and 
hospitals in the Crimea peninsula and in Sakhalin.
Due to its exceptionally high balneological properties volcanic 
mud is successfully used by the medics in for treating many 
maladies such as diseases of locomotor system, joints, spine, 
peripheral nervous system, skin, gastroenteric tract, diabetes, 
atherosclerosis and cervical osteochondrosis, in gynecology, 
urology and cosmetology.
Chemically this mud mainly consists of silica (55-70%). At the 
same time it has ingredients that are quite beneficial for health: 
iodine, borate, bromine, calcium, magnesium, chloride, lithium, 
iron, selenium, manganese, zinc, etc. Spectral analysis of volcanic 
mud found over 20 chemical elements. Such organic substances as 
humic and ftilvic acids, naphthenic acids, resins, asphaltens, 
methane, naphthenic and aromatic hydrocarbons, oils, etc. were 
found in small concentrations in the mud. This mud has similar 
organic composition with silt mud and healing Naphthalane oil. 
Among organic substances biologically active substances deserve
128 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev W HAT DO W E K N O W  A B O U T M UD V O LC A N O E S ? 129
the primary attention and metaboric acids that have bactericidal 
action.
The solution of mount mud is a clear liquid with yellowish 
shade without smell and with salty taste. Mineralization of mud 
solution of mud volcanoes (10-40 g/1) is low in comparison with silt 
mud (150-350 g/1).
The results of experiments allowed to recommend mud solution 
of mud volcanoes as a new mud preparation designed for 
electrophoresis treatment of different diseases.
It is rather interesting that as far back as in the 80s of the last 
century we jointly with medics of Baku introduced volcanic mud in 
the practical application of more than 15 medical institutions. In 
addition, in a number of Azerbaijan regions local population on its 
own initiative takes mud baths directly on volcanoes using the 
"Egyptian" mud therapy methods. People on volcano Bakhar in the 
Alat area of the Caspian coast using the vicinity of the sea combine 
mud therapy with subsequent hydrotherapeutic procedures (photo 
31,32).
Photo 31. Healing volcanic mud
130 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 32. Mud solutions is a medicinal preparation
Azerbaijan has very large reserves of this valuable mud. There 
are conditions for its wide-scale application, organization of a 
centralized mud therapy clinic even on the Caspian coast where 
large volcanoes are situated. This mud therapy clinic can become a 
health resort in the natural conditions.
Currently, the muds of Bulganak volcano are used in the clinics 
of Feodosia and Kerch. The history of application of volcanic mud 
here started as far back as in the 30s of the last century.
Thus, the regions of development of mud volcanoes in the future 
can become the areas of deployment of a wide network of mud 
therapy clinics. It is necessary to use the opportunities given by the 
nature to doctors that creating a valuable medical preparation in its 
natural laboratories.
W HAT DO W E KN O W  A B O U T M U D  V O LC A N O E S ? 131
XII. MUD VOLCANO IS A UNIQUE NATURAL
MONUMENT
Mud volcano is a unique natural phenomenon that is 
distinguished by an unusual “lunar” landscape, peculiar beauty, 
continuous dormant state and rare but formidable disastrous 
eruptions accompanied by fire flares. Careful attitude to these 
natural phenomena, preservation of intact mud volcanic landscapes 
for the future generations is one of the most relevant tasks. It is 
especially important in connection with numerous known facts of 
littering of gryphons, setting up of waste dumps in the calderas of 
steppe volcanoes, uncontrollable use of mud volcanic breccias as a 
construction material and chemical raw material. Such acts do not 
only result in the extermination of this natural phenomena but they 
are also antisanitaric and hazardous for the environment to a certain 
degree because they do not take into account the activity of mud 
volcanoes, peculiar mechanism of this process leading to 
dissemination and scattering of mud volcanic materials and of all 
potential contaminants.
Mud volcanoes is a national property and natural resource of our 
country. For this reason we are obliged to take care of them and try 
to use as much as possible everything that is given to us by nature 
without any special costs.
The State Preserve of a group of mud volcanoes situated in the 
Absheron peninsula and Gobustan was created in August 2007 by 
the decision of the President of Azerbaijan Republic.
Mud volcano state preserve in Azerbaijan that is a motherland of 
mud volcanoes is not just a geological national park preventing 
engineering operations and construction, production of mineral 
resources, disposal of waste, it implies comprehensive protection of 
geological and biological environment in the most interesting areas 
of development of mud volcanism on the largest, the most 
picturesque and peculiar mud volcanoes.
Mud volcanoes is a source of richness and great attraction for 
ecotourism. In the countries that have volcanoes including mud
132
volcanoes they are used for tourist routes generating significant 
profit. It is possible to organize many tourist routes in Azerbaijan 
especially in the areas to south of Baku. Volcanoes here form entire 
landscape lining up as if they are prepared for a parade. Widely 
known world's champion in terms of the number of eruptions 
Lökbatan volcano that is closely linked with the history of oil 
production in Azerbaijan, magnificent 400 m high giants 
Otmanbozdag, Beyuk, Kanizadag, Touragai volcanoes, large 
volcanoes on the Caspian coast - Bakhar, Khamamdag. We have 
volcanoes situated in the picturesque places, for example, Demirchi 
(photo 33) in Shamakha district to the north of Pirkuli or Dashgil 
(photo 34) near the Gobustan State cultural-historical -  Artistic 
Preserve and many other beautiful, active spectacular volcanoes - 
surely, we cannot enumerate all of them.
Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 33. Damirchi mud volcano
Mud volcanoes are interesting not only for geologists but also 
nature-lovers, naturalists. Significant attention to Azerbaijan 
volcanoes, interest to this natural phenomenon is expressed by
W HAT DO W E K N O W  A B O U T M UD V O LC AN O ES ? 133
foreigners, employees of oil companies who work in Baku, foreign 
scientists and the majority of tourists who visit our country 
(photo 35).
Photo 34. Dashgil mud volcano
This was a reason to publish a brochure and guidebook Mud 
Volcanoes of Azerbaijan written by Ad.A.Aliyev in the Azeri, 
Russian and English. It described 25 mud volcanoes that can be 
interesting for tourists.
Tourist trips to mud volcanoes naturally can become of source 
of foreign currency inflow as it is the case in other countries. Mud 
volcanoes can be attractive for the tourism business also because 
volcanic mud used by the medics has exceptionally high 
balneological properties and our country has inexhaustible reserves 
of this mud.
In the conclusion it is necessary to note that there is a long­
standing need to set up research stations on some volcanoes for 
monitoring of their activity.
134 Ad.A.Aliyev, I.S.Guliyev, A.A.Feyzullayev
Photo 35. Pirekishkyu/  mud volcano
It would allow to study the possibility of prediction of hazardous 
eruptions of volcanoes and their mechanism, it would resolve many 
fundamental problems of the general and oil and gas geology, etc. 
Such stations would become a good facility for internship of 
students-geologists.
In our opinion an idea of creation a museum of mud volcanism 
is also quite attractive. Such museum would collect all available 
materials about this unique natural phenomenon and exhibit all 
currently available mineralogical, lithological and other discoveries 
as well as the models of formation of mud volcanoes and their 
activities.
